AI Analysis — 4.20-e2e-telco5g-ptp

AI Analysis

TL;DR: Cluster log-stream collapse + API auth expiry wiped 22 of 24 tests; a linuxptp-daemon state-machine regression caused the remaining 2 TGM holdover failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 12/24 failures — linuxptp-daemon log stream unreachable (ClockSync GetProfileLogID/GetClockIDForeign timeout): All ClockSync tests in bc (3), dualfollower (3), dualnicbc (3), dualnicbcha (2), and oc-serial test 1 (1) hit could not find regex in log stream … error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded or timedout waiting for matches. The test helper opens a live kubectl logs --follow stream and waits for a ptp4l profile or sync line that never arrives within 3–10 minutes. Two compounding factors: (a) ptp4l may not be reaching SLAVE state cluster-wide (no grandmaster reachable or log format changed by PR #613), and (b) when the API server began degrading, streaming connections were silently severed rather than cleanly refused.

• 10/24 failures — Kubernetes API server Unauthorized mid-run (oc-serial tests 2–11): After the first oc-serial test completed at ~07:29 UTC, the kubeconfig credentials expired or the API server rejected them (Unauthorized / couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials). Every subsequent test aborted immediately at the DaemonSet readiness check (linuxptp-daemon DaemonSet must exist before readiness wait → Unauthorized). One variant also showed dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: connection refused, indicating the API server briefly went fully unreachable.

• 2/24 failures — TGM holdover state-machine regression (tgm suite): Both T-GM holdover tests fail deterministically: disabling GNSS causes ts2phcState to be forced to PTP_FREERUN (not PTP_HOLDOVER) when NoSourceTSCount == 2 in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/event/event.go:402–403, making ClockClass 7 unreachable. Test 1 exhausted its 3-minute poll; test 2 observed map[metric:248] (freerun) throughout the 10-second sampling window. This is a deterministic regression, not a flake.


Cross-Suite Patterns:


PatternSuites affected
GetProfileLogID / GetClockIDForeign log stream timeoutbc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, oc (test 1)
API server Unauthorized cascadeoc (tests 2–11)
GNSS → ClockClass 7 holdover state-machine bugtgm

The log-stream failures are 100% cross-suite (5 of 6 suites, identical error text, different pod names) — confirming a cluster-wide cause rather than a suite-specific issue. The oc Unauthorized failures are oc-specific but are a secondary consequence of the same cluster degradation event. The tgm failures are suite-specific and code-driven.


No suite is entirely clean. dualnicbcha is the only suite where the log-stream failure count is below its total suite size (2 of 2 failed; no "passing" baseline in that suite either).



Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job immediately and monitor the PTP grandmaster. The log-stream and API-auth failures bear all hallmarks of a transient lab infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, credential rotation, API server instability on telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com around 2026-06-24 07:00–08:30 UTC). A clean re-run will confirm whether the 22 non-TGM failures are infra flakes.

2. Audit linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0, "upstream-sync-2026-06-22") for ptp4l log-format changes. If the upstream sync altered the format of the Ptp4lConf: or selected best master clock log lines, the test regexes in ptphelper.go and pods.go will never match regardless of cluster health. Compare the ptp4l log output from a pre-PR-613 build against a post-PR-613 pod to confirm or rule out a log-format regression.

3. Fix the TGM holdover state machine in event.go:402–403. Remove or guard the unconditional ts2phcState = PTP_FREERUN override when NoSourceTSCount == 2; instead, allow the state to transition to PTP_HOLDOVER so the existing ClockClass 7 branch at lines 459–461 and 430–433 becomes reachable. This is a deterministic code regression and will not self-heal with a re-run.


Overall Issue Class: infra_other (dominant — 22/24 failures) with an embedded test_regression (2/24 tgm failures from PR #613 state-machine change)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — the entire 24-test job failed; the cluster experienced mid-run auth collapse, and a code regression in the TGM holdover path is deterministic and will recur on every re-run.




Per-Suite Details



bc



Suite: bc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests failed because Kubernetes log streaming to linuxptp-daemon pods returned context deadline exceeded / timeout errors during the GetProfileLogID step, preventing the test from locating the ptp4l config log line needed to derive the foreign master clock ID.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Kubernetes pod log stream failure in GetProfileLogID (affects: all 3 tests — "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-fpgx7 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

From the detailed agent logs (prior identical run same day, pod linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg):

```

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 1 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 2 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptptesthelper.go: 68] GetClockIDForeign retry due to err: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

Additionally, the API server was returning Unauthorized by 08:29 UTC (end of job), with the bc ClockSync tests running at 07:02–08:29 UTC — indicating progressive auth/credential degradation throughout the long 3.5-hour job:

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

E0624 08:29:47.118913 memcache.go:265] "Unhandled Error" err="couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials"

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetProfileLogID in test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go opens a live Kubernetes log stream (Follow: true, no TailLines) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex searching for the regex (?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: (.|\n)?message_tag \[([^\]]*)\] within a 3-minute timeout. The stream — opened with context.TODO() so no test-side deadline — is being terminated by the infrastructure with context deadline exceeded before the regex can be matched. This error pattern repeats identically across all ClockSync tests in bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, and dualnicbcha suites, confirming a cluster-wide log streaming connectivity issue rather than a daemon log format regression. The linuxptp-daemon does emit this log line (printNodeProfile in pkg/daemon/daemon.go:1369 writes the rendered Ptp4lConf with #profile: prefix and message_tag), but the HTTP connection carrying the pod log stream is dropped before the data reaches the test. The progressive Unauthorized failures at job end suggest the kubeconfig token was near expiry, which may also have disrupted API server proxy connections to node kubelets mid-run.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — no daemon code change identified; the failure is infrastructure-side log stream connectivity.
• Is it a flake? Yes
• Suggested Fix: Retry GetPodLogsRegex with exponential backoff on context deadline exceeded / stream errors (already partially attempted per ptphelper.go:123 retry log) and add a SinceSeconds window to avoid streaming large log volumes. Also investigate whether the telco5g bare-metal cluster's API server → kubelet log proxy connections are being cut by an intermediate timeout (check keepalive/idle settings on the cluster's internal load balancer).

Suite Issue Class: infra_timeout

Suite Severity: MEDIUM


dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the test helper GetProfileLogID could not find the Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1 log marker in linuxptp-daemon-9cv64's container logs — that entry was rotated out ~40 minutes before the tests ran.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Profile log entry lost to container log rotation (affects: all 3 tests — Slave can sync to master, Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down, Can provide a profile with higher priority)

• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded [tests 1 & 2]


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=timedout waiting for matches [test 3]

```

Test wall-clock timeouts (~201 s, ~205 s, ~207 s) are consistent with a 3-minute GetProfileLogID Pass-2 follow timeout (180 s) plus overhead. The dualfollower suite started at 05:45:01; the operator/daemon was deployed at ~05:05:33 — a gap of ~40 minutes.


The same failure pattern (could not get any profile line) hits every other suite in this run (bc → linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8/fpgx7; dualnicbc → linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q/4cmtj; dualnicbcha → linuxptp-daemon-8fk9k/mt258). All are cross-suite, cross-pod, and trigger the identical error path, confirming a systemic cause.


• Root Cause: BasicClockSyncCheck in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:60 calls GetClockIDForeign → GetProfileLogID (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:69), which scans linuxptp-daemon-container logs for the regex:

```

(?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1(.|\n)?message_tag \[(.*)\]

```

The daemon emits this line exactly once — inside applyNodePtpProfile → printNodeProfile → printWhenNotNil(nodeProfile.Ptp4lConf, "Ptp4lConf") at daemon.go:1369, called only when a ptpconfig is (re)applied. By 05:45, ptp4l + phc2sys have logged ~1 line/s for ~40 minutes; the early Ptp4lConf: entry has been rotated out of the container log visible to the Kubernetes GetLogs API. GetPodLogsRegex Pass 1 (snapshot, test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214) finds nothing; Pass 2 (follow, 3-minute context at pods.go:254) waits fruitlessly because the daemon never re-logs the profile until reconfigured, exhausting the timeout (pods.go:153 for tests 1–2, pods.go:167 for test 3), which bubbles up as ptphelper.go:83 "could not get any profile line".


• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the log-rotation exposure is a pre-existing test design limitation; no single PR is directly identifiable from available evidence. The most recent structural changes near this code path are 9be567c (2026-05-07, "refactor: Remove unused functions and enhance PTP configuration logic") and 0f98a60 (2026-01-14, "fixed ci blocker: added context timeout to GetLogsPodRegex") on the ptp-operator main branch; either could have affected how long Pass-1/Pass-2 tolerates missing entries. The release-4.20 branch merge history is not available locally to confirm backport.

• Is it a flake? No — all 3 tests in this suite failed, and the exact same pattern repeats across every other non-oc suite in the same run. This is a systematic failure.

• Suggested Fix: Change GetProfileLogID to periodically re-trigger the Ptp4lConf: log entry (e.g., by forcing a no-op ptpconfig update to restart reconciliation), or redesign the profile-ID lookup to not rely on a one-shot log event that may be rotated — for example, read it from the live PtpConfig CR spec and derive the messageTag from the known naming scheme (ptp4l..config:{level}), which is deterministic and does not require log scanning.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the linuxptp-daemon containers never emitted the selected best master clock log line, indicating PTP synchronization was never achieved on the test cluster nodes.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: linuxptp-daemon not achieving PTP clock synchronization (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-4cmtj container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches

```

And from the build log post-run (gathering phase):

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

error: creating temp namespace: Unauthorized

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetClockIDForeign() (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:127-151) scans the linuxptp-daemon-container log stream for the regex (?m)\[%s\]. selected best master clock (.) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex() (test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214-269), which internally calls findRegexInStream() (pods.go:141-171) with a 10-minute timeout. This line is only emitted by ptp4l when it successfully selects a grandmaster/best master; since it never appeared in any daemon pod across all ptpconfigs (test-bc-master1, test-slave1, temp), the PTP daemon was not achieving clock synchronization. Critically, the identical "could not find regex in log stream" error hit all ClockSync tests across bc-serial, dualfollower-serial, dualnicbcha-serial, and dualnicbc-serial as well — indicating a cluster-wide failure to synchronize PTP, most likely caused by the telco5g lab's physical grandmaster being unreachable during this CI run rather than a code regression.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the most recent linuxptp-daemon commit is 0459bc0 (upstream-sync-2026-06-22) and the ptp-operator test repo shows 3586177 ("ci: add ginkgo flake mitigation and fix higher-priority test"). No log-format changes were observed that would break the regex. The failure is consistent with an infra/lab connectivity issue.
• Is it a flake? Yes — the cross-suite, cross-pod, cross-node uniformity of the timeout (all suites hit the same pattern) strongly indicates a transient infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, PTP network disruption in the telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com lab cluster) rather than a deterministic code regression. The oc-serial tests that ran later additionally hit Unauthorized / connection refused to the API server (10.8.34.117:6443), further confirming the lab cluster was degraded during this run.
• Suggested Fix: Re-run the nightly job to confir

dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (3 failures)

Critically, the identical "could not find regex in log stream" error hit all ClockSync tests across bc-serial, dualfollower-serial, dualnicbcha-serial, and dualnicbc-serial as well — indicating a cluster-wide failure to synchronize PTP, most likely caused by the telco5g lab's physical grandmaster being unreachable during this CI run rather than a code regression.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the most recent linuxptp-daemon commit is 0459bc0 (upstream-sync-2026-06-22) and the ptp-operator test repo shows 3586177 ("ci: add ginkgo flake mitigation and fix higher-priority test"). No log-format changes were observed that would break the regex. The failure is consistent with an infra/lab connectivity issue.
• Is it a flake? Yes — the cross-suite, cross-pod, cross-node uniformity of the timeout (all suites hit the same pattern) strongly indicates a transient infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, PTP network disruption in the telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com lab cluster) rather than a deterministic code regression. The oc-serial tests that ran later additionally hit Unauthorized / connection refused to the API server (10.8.34.117:6443), further confirming the lab cluster was degraded during this run.
• Suggested Fix: Re-run the nightly job to confir


TL;DR: Cluster log-stream collapse + API auth expiry wiped 22 of 24 tests; a linuxptp-daemon state-machine regression caused the remaining 2 TGM holdover failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 12/24 failures — linuxptp-daemon log stream unreachable (ClockSync GetProfileLogID/GetClockIDForeign timeout): All ClockSync tests in bc (3), dualfollower (3), dualnicbc (3), dualnicbcha (2), and oc-serial test 1 (1) hit could not find regex in log stream … error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded or timedout waiting for matches. The test helper opens a live kubectl logs --follow stream and waits for a ptp4l profile or sync line that never arrives within 3–10 minutes. Two compounding factors: (a) ptp4l may not be reaching SLAVE state cluster-wide (no grandmaster reachable or log format changed by PR #613), and (b) when the API server began degrading, streaming connections were silently severed rather than cleanly refused.

• 10/24 failures — Kubernetes API server Unauthorized mid-run (oc-serial tests 2–11): After the first oc-serial test completed at ~07:29 UTC, the kubeconfig credentials expired or the API server rejected them (Unauthorized / couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials). Every subsequent test aborted immediately at the DaemonSet readiness check (linuxptp-daemon DaemonSet must exist before readiness wait → Unauthorized). One variant also showed dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: connection refused, indicating the API server briefly went fully unreachable.

• 2/24 failures — TGM holdover state-machine regression (tgm suite): Both T-GM holdover tests fail deterministically: disabling GNSS causes ts2phcState to be forced to PTP_FREERUN (not PTP_HOLDOVER) when NoSourceTSCount == 2 in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/event/event.go:402–403, making ClockClass 7 unreachable. Test 1 exhausted its 3-minute poll; test 2 observed map[metric:248] (freerun) throughout the 10-second sampling window. This is a deterministic regression, not a flake.


Cross-Suite Patterns:


PatternSuites affected
GetProfileLogID / GetClockIDForeign log stream timeoutbc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, oc (test 1)
API server Unauthorized cascadeoc (tests 2–11)
GNSS → ClockClass 7 holdover state-machine bugtgm

The log-stream failures are 100% cross-suite (5 of 6 suites, identical error text, different pod names) — confirming a cluster-wide cause rather than a suite-specific issue. The oc Unauthorized failures are oc-specific but are a secondary consequence of the same cluster degradation event. The tgm failures are suite-specific and code-driven.


No suite is entirely clean. dualnicbcha is the only suite where the log-stream failure count is below its total suite size (2 of 2 failed; no "passing" baseline in that suite either).



Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job immediately and monitor the PTP grandmaster. The log-stream and API-auth failures bear all hallmarks of a transient lab infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, credential rotation, API server instability on telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com around 2026-06-24 07:00–08:30 UTC). A clean re-run will confirm whether the 22 non-TGM failures are infra flakes.

2. Audit linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0, "upstream-sync-2026-06-22") for ptp4l log-format changes. If the upstream sync altered the format of the Ptp4lConf: or selected best master clock log lines, the test regexes in ptphelper.go and pods.go will never match regardless of cluster health. Compare the ptp4l log output from a pre-PR-613 build against a post-PR-613 pod to confirm or rule out a log-format regression.

3. Fix the TGM holdover state machine in event.go:402–403. Remove or guard the unconditional ts2phcState = PTP_FREERUN override when NoSourceTSCount == 2; instead, allow the state to transition to PTP_HOLDOVER so the existing ClockClass 7 branch at lines 459–461 and 430–433 becomes reachable. This is a deterministic code regression and will not self-heal with a re-run.


Overall Issue Class: infra_other (dominant — 22/24 failures) with an embedded test_regression (2/24 tgm failures from PR #613 state-machine change)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — the entire 24-test job failed; the cluster experienced mid-run auth collapse, and a code regression in the TGM holdover path is deterministic and will recur on every re-run.




Per-Suite Details



bc



Suite: bc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests failed because Kubernetes log streaming to linuxptp-daemon pods returned context deadline exceeded / timeout errors during the GetProfileLogID step, preventing the test from locating the ptp4l config log line needed to derive the foreign master clock ID.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Kubernetes pod log stream failure in GetProfileLogID (affects: all 3 tests — "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-fpgx7 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

From the detailed agent logs (prior identical run same day, pod linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg):

```

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 1 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 2 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptptesthelper.go: 68] GetClockIDForeign retry due to err: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

Additionally, the API server was returning Unauthorized by 08:29 UTC (end of job), with the bc ClockSync tests running at 07:02–08:29 UTC — indicating progressive auth/credential degradation throughout the long 3.5-hour job:

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

E0624 08:29:47.118913 memcache.go:265] "Unhandled Error" err="couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials"

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetProfileLogID in test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go opens a live Kubernetes log stream (Follow: true, no TailLines) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex searching for the regex (?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: (.|\n)?message_tag \[([^\]]*)\] within a 3-minute timeout. The stream — opened with context.TODO() so no test-side deadline — is being terminated by the infrastructure with context deadline exceeded before the regex can be matched. This error pattern repeats identically across all ClockSync tests in bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, and dualnicbcha suites, confirming a cluster-wide log streaming connectivity issue rather than a daemon log format regression. The linuxptp-daemon does emit this log line (printNodeProfile in pkg/daemon/daemon.go:1369 writes the rendered Ptp4lConf with #profile: prefix and message_tag), but the HTTP connection carrying the pod log stream is dropped before the data reaches the test. The progressive Unauthorized failures at job end suggest the kubeconfig token was near expiry, which may also have disrupted API server proxy connections to node kubelets mid-run.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — no daemon code change identified; the failure is infrastructure-side log stream connectivity.
• Is it a flake? Yes
• Suggested Fix: Retry GetPodLogsRegex with exponential backoff on context deadline exceeded / stream errors (already partially attempted per ptphelper.go:123 retry log) and add a SinceSeconds window to avoid streaming large log volumes. Also investigate whether the telco5g bare-metal cluster's API server → kubelet log proxy connections are being cut by an intermediate timeout (check keepalive/idle settings on the cluster's internal load balancer).

Suite Issue Class: infra_timeout

Suite Severity: MEDIUM


dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the test helper GetProfileLogID could not find the Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1 log marker in linuxptp-daemon-9cv64's container logs — that entry was rotated out ~40 minutes before the tests ran.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Profile log entry lost to container log rotation (affects: all 3 tests — Slave can sync to master, Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down, Can provide a profile with higher priority)

• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded [tests 1 & 2]


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=timedout waiting for matches [test 3]

```

Test wall-clock timeouts (~201 s, ~205 s, ~207 s) are consistent with a 3-minute GetProfileLogID Pass-2 follow timeout (180 s) plus overhead. The dualfollower suite started at 05:45:01; the operator/daemon was deployed at ~05:05:33 — a gap of ~40 minutes.


The same failure pattern (could not get any profile line) hits every other suite in this run (bc → linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8/fpgx7; dualnicbc → linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q/4cmtj; dualnicbcha → linuxptp-daemon-8fk9k/mt258). All are cross-suite, cross-pod, and trigger the identical error path, confirming a systemic cause.


• Root Cause: BasicClockSyncCheck in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:60 calls GetClockIDForeign → GetProfileLogID (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:69), which scans linuxptp-daemon-container logs for the regex:

```

(?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1(.|\n)?message_tag \[(.*)\]

```

The daemon emits this line exactly once — inside applyNodePtpProfile → printNodeProfile → printWhenNotNil(nodeProfile.Ptp4lConf, "Ptp4lConf") at daemon.go:1369, called only when a ptpconfig is (re)applied. By 05:45, ptp4l + phc2sys have logged ~1 line/s for ~40 minutes; the early Ptp4lConf: entry has been rotated out of the container log visible to the Kubernetes GetLogs API. GetPodLogsRegex Pass 1 (snapshot, test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214) finds nothing; Pass 2 (follow, 3-minute context at pods.go:254) waits fruitlessly because the daemon never re-logs the profile until reconfigured, exhausting the timeout (pods.go:153 for tests 1–2, pods.go:167 for test 3), which bubbles up as ptphelper.go:83 "could not get any profile line".


• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the log-rotation exposure is a pre-existing test design limitation; no single PR is directly identifiable from available evidence. The most recent structural changes near this code path are 9be567c (2026-05-07, "refactor: Remove unused functions and enhance PTP configuration logic") and 0f98a60 (2026-01-14, "fixed ci blocker: added context timeout to GetLogsPodRegex") on the ptp-operator main branch; either could have affected how long Pass-1/Pass-2 tolerates missing entries. The release-4.20 branch merge history is not available locally to confirm backport.

• Is it a flake? No — all 3 tests in this suite failed, and the exact same pattern repeats across every other non-oc suite in the same run. This is a systematic failure.

• Suggested Fix: Change GetProfileLogID to periodically re-trigger the Ptp4lConf: log entry (e.g., by forcing a no-op ptpconfig update to restart reconciliation), or redesign the profile-ID lookup to not rely on a one-shot log event that may be rotated — for example, read it from the live PtpConfig CR spec and derive the messageTag from the known naming scheme (ptp4l..config:{level}), which is deterministic and does not require log scanning.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH

• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-4cmtj container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches

```

And from the build log post-run (gathering phase):

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

error: creating temp namespace: Unauthorized

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetClockIDForeign() (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:127-151) scans the linuxptp-daemon-container log stream for the regex (?m)\[%s\]. selected best master clock (.) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex() (test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214-269), which internally calls findRegexInStream() (pods.go:141-171) with a 10-minute timeout. This line is only emitted by ptp4l when it successfully selects a grandmaster/best master; since it never appeared in any daemon pod across all ptpconfigs (test-bc-master1, test-slave1, temp), the PTP daemon was not achieving clock synchronization. Critically, the identical "could not find regex in log stream" error hit all ClockSync tests across bc-serial, dualfollower-serial, dualnicbcha-serial, and dualnicbc-serial as well — indicating a cluster-wide failure to synchronize PTP, most likely caused by the telco5g lab's physical grandmaster being unreachable during this CI run rather than a code regression.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the most recent linuxptp-daemon commit is 0459bc0 (upstream-sync-2026-06-22) and the ptp-operator test repo shows 3586177 ("ci: add ginkgo flake mitigation and fix higher-priority test"). No log-format changes were observed that would break the regex. The failure is consistent with an infra/lab connectivity issue.
• Is it a flake? Yes — the cross-suite, cross-pod, cross-node uniformity of the timeout (all suites hit the same pattern) strongly indicates a transient infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, PTP network disruption in the telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com lab cluster) rather than a deterministic code regression. The oc-serial tests that ran later additionally hit Unauthorized / connection refused to the API server (10.8.34.117:6443), further confirming the lab cluster was degraded during this run.
• Suggested Fix: Re-run the nightly job to confir


TL;DR: Cluster log-stream collapse + API auth expiry wiped 22 of 24 tests; a linuxptp-daemon state-machine regression caused the remaining 2 TGM holdover failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 12/24 failures — linuxptp-daemon log stream unreachable (ClockSync GetProfileLogID/GetClockIDForeign timeout): All ClockSync tests in bc (3), dualfollower (3), dualnicbc (3), dualnicbcha (2), and oc-serial test 1 (1) hit could not find regex in log stream … error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded or timedout waiting for matches. The test helper opens a live kubectl logs --follow stream and waits for a ptp4l profile or sync line that never arrives within 3–10 minutes. Two compounding factors: (a) ptp4l may not be reaching SLAVE state cluster-wide (no grandmaster reachable or log format changed by PR #613), and (b) when the API server began degrading, streaming connections were silently severed rather than cleanly refused.

• 10/24 failures — Kubernetes API server Unauthorized mid-run (oc-serial tests 2–11): After the first oc-serial test completed at ~07:29 UTC, the kubeconfig credentials expired or the API server rejected them (Unauthorized / couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials). Every subsequent test aborted immediately at the DaemonSet readiness check (linuxptp-daemon DaemonSet must exist before readiness wait → Unauthorized). One variant also showed dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: connection refused, indicating the API server briefly went fully unreachable.

• 2/24 failures — TGM holdover state-machine regression (tgm suite): Both T-GM holdover tests fail deterministically: disabling GNSS causes ts2phcState to be forced to PTP_FREERUN (not PTP_HOLDOVER) when NoSourceTSCount == 2 in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/event/event.go:402–403, making ClockClass 7 unreachable. Test 1 exhausted its 3-minute poll; test 2 observed map[metric:248] (freerun) throughout the 10-second sampling window. This is a deterministic regression, not a flake.


Cross-Suite Patterns:


PatternSuites affected
GetProfileLogID / GetClockIDForeign log stream timeoutbc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, oc (test 1)
API server Unauthorized cascadeoc (tests 2–11)
GNSS → ClockClass 7 holdover state-machine bugtgm

The log-stream failures are 100% cross-suite (5 of 6 suites, identical error text, different pod names) — confirming a cluster-wide cause rather than a suite-specific issue. The oc Unauthorized failures are oc-specific but are a secondary consequence of the same cluster degradation event. The tgm failures are suite-specific and code-driven.


No suite is entirely clean. dualnicbcha is the only suite where the log-stream failure count is below its total suite size (2 of 2 failed; no "passing" baseline in that suite either).



Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job immediately and monitor the PTP grandmaster. The log-stream and API-auth failures bear all hallmarks of a transient lab infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, credential rotation, API server instability on telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com around 2026-06-24 07:00–08:30 UTC). A clean re-run will confirm whether the 22 non-TGM failures are infra flakes.

2. Audit linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0, "upstream-sync-2026-06-22") for ptp4l log-format changes. If the upstream sync altered the format of the Ptp4lConf: or selected best master clock log lines, the test regexes in ptphelper.go and pods.go will never match regardless of cluster health. Compare the ptp4l log output from a pre-PR-613 build against a post-PR-613 pod to confirm or rule out a log-format regression.

3. Fix the TGM holdover state machine in event.go:402–403. Remove or guard the unconditional ts2phcState = PTP_FREERUN override when NoSourceTSCount == 2; instead, allow the state to transition to PTP_HOLDOVER so the existing ClockClass 7 branch at lines 459–461 and 430–433 becomes reachable. This is a deterministic code regression and will not self-heal with a re-run.


Overall Issue Class: infra_other (dominant — 22/24 failures) with an embedded test_regression (2/24 tgm failures from PR #613 state-machine change)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — the entire 24-test job failed; the cluster experienced mid-run auth collapse, and a code regression in the TGM holdover path is deterministic and will recur on every re-run.




Per-Suite Details



bc



Suite: bc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests failed because Kubernetes log streaming to linuxptp-daemon pods returned context deadline exceeded / timeout errors during the GetProfileLogID step, preventing the test from locating the ptp4l config log line needed to derive the foreign master clock ID.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Kubernetes pod log stream failure in GetProfileLogID (affects: all 3 tests — "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-fpgx7 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

From the detailed agent logs (prior identical run same day, pod linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg):

```

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 1 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 2 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptptesthelper.go: 68] GetClockIDForeign retry due to err: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

Additionally, the API server was returning Unauthorized by 08:29 UTC (end of job), with the bc ClockSync tests running at 07:02–08:29 UTC — indicating progressive auth/credential degradation throughout the long 3.5-hour job:

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

E0624 08:29:47.118913 memcache.go:265] "Unhandled Error" err="couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials"

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetProfileLogID in test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go opens a live Kubernetes log stream (Follow: true, no TailLines) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex searching for the regex (?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: (.|\n)?message_tag \[([^\]]*)\] within a 3-minute timeout. The stream — opened with context.TODO() so no test-side deadline — is being terminated by the infrastructure with context deadline exceeded before the regex can be matched. This error pattern repeats identically across all ClockSync tests in bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, and dualnicbcha suites, confirming a cluster-wide log streaming connectivity issue rather than a daemon log format regression. The linuxptp-daemon does emit this log line (printNodeProfile in pkg/daemon/daemon.go:1369 writes the rendered Ptp4lConf with #profile: prefix and message_tag), but the HTTP connection carrying the pod log stream is dropped before the data reaches the test. The progressive Unauthorized failures at job end suggest the kubeconfig token was near expiry, which may also have disrupted API server proxy connections to node kubelets mid-run.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — no daemon code change identified; the failure is infrastructure-side log stream connectivity.
• Is it a flake? Yes
• Suggested Fix: Retry GetPodLogsRegex with exponential backoff on context deadline exceeded / stream errors (already partially attempted per ptphelper.go:123 retry log) and add a SinceSeconds window to avoid streaming large log volumes. Also investigate whether the telco5g bare-metal cluster's API server → kubelet log proxy connections are being cut by an intermediate timeout (check keepalive/idle settings on the cluster's internal load balancer).

Suite Issue Class: infra_timeout

Suite Severity: MEDIUM


dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the test helper GetProfileLogID could not find the Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1 log marker in linuxptp-daemon-9cv64's container logs — that entry was rotated out ~40 minutes before the tests ran.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Profile log entry lost to container log rotation (affects: all 3 tests — Slave can sync to master, Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down, Can provide a profile with higher priority)

• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded [tests 1 & 2]


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=timedout waiting for matches [test 3]

```

Test wall-clock timeouts (~201 s, ~205 s, ~207 s) are consistent with a 3-minute GetProfileLogID Pass-2 follow timeout (180 s) plus overhead. The dualfollower suite started at 05:45:01; the operator/daemon was deployed at ~05:05:33 — a gap of ~40 minutes.


The same failure pattern (could not get any profile line) hits every other suite in this run (bc → linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8/fpgx7; dualnicbc → linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q/4cmtj; dualnicbcha → linuxptp-daemon-8fk9k/mt258). All are cross-suite, cross-pod, and trigger the identical error path, confirming a systemic cause.


• Root Cause: BasicClockSyncCheck in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:60 calls GetClockIDForeign → GetProfileLogID (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:69), which scans linuxptp-daemon-container logs for the regex:

```

(?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1(.|\n)?message_tag \[(.*)\]

```

The daemon emits this line exactly once — inside applyNodePtpProfile → printNodeProfile → printWhenNotNil(nodeProfile.Ptp4lConf, "Ptp4lConf") at daemon.go:1369, called only when a ptpconfig is (re)applied. By 05:45, ptp4l + phc2sys have logged ~1 line/s for ~40 minutes; the early Ptp4lConf: entry has been rotated out of the container log visible to the Kubernetes GetLogs API. GetPodLogsRegex Pass 1 (snapshot, test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214) finds nothing; Pass 2 (follow, 3-minute context at pods.go:254) waits fruitlessly because the daemon never re-logs the profile until reconfigured, exhausting the timeout (pods.go:153 for tests 1–2, pods.go:167 for test 3), which bubbles up as ptphelper.go:83 "could not get any profile line".


• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the log-rotation exposure is a pre-existing test design limitation; no single PR is directly identifiable from available evidence. The most recent structural changes near this code path are 9be567c (2026-05-07, "refactor: Remove unused functions and enhance PTP configuration logic") and 0f98a60 (2026-01-14, "fixed ci blocker: added context timeout to GetLogsPodRegex") on the ptp-operator main branch; either could have affected how long Pass-1/Pass-2 tolerates missing entries. The release-4.20 branch merge history is not available locally to confirm backport.

• Is it a flake? No — all 3 tests in this suite failed, and the exact same pattern repeats across every other non-oc suite in the same run. This is a systematic failure.

• Suggested Fix: Change GetProfileLogID to periodically re-trigger the Ptp4lConf: log entry (e.g., by forcing a no-op ptpconfig update to restart reconciliation), or redesign the profile-ID lookup to not rely on a one-shot log event that may be rotated — for example, read it from the live PtpConfig CR spec and derive the messageTag from the known naming scheme (ptp4l..config:{level}), which is deterministic and does not require log scanning.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH

• Suggested Fix: Change GetProfileLogID to periodically re-trigger the Ptp4lConf: log entry (e.g., by forcing a no-op ptpconfig update to restart reconciliation), or redesign the profile-ID lookup to not rely on a one-shot log event that may be rotated — for example, read it from the live PtpConfig CR spec and derive the messageTag from the known naming scheme (ptp4l..config:{level}), which is deterministic and does not require log scanning.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the linuxptp-daemon containers never emitted the selected best master clock log line, indicating PTP synchronization was never achieved on the test cluster nodes.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: linuxptp-daemon not achieving PTP clock synchronization (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-4cmtj container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches

```

And from the build log post-run (gathering phase):

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

error: creating temp namespace: Unauthorized

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetClockIDForeign() (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:127-151) scans the linuxptp-daemon-container log stream for the regex (?m)\[%s\]. selected best master clock (.) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex() (test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214-269), which internally calls findRegexInStream() (pods.go:141-171) with a 10-minute timeout. This line is only emitted by ptp4l when it successfully selects a grandmaster/best master; since it never appeared in any daemon pod across all ptpconfigs (test-bc-master1, test-slave1, temp), the PTP daemon was not achieving clock synchronization. Critically, the identical "could not find regex in log stream" error hit all ClockSync tests across bc-serial, dualfollower-serial, dualnicbcha-serial, and dualnicbc-serial as well — indicating a cluster-wide failure to synchronize PTP, most likely caused by the telco5g lab's physical grandmaster being unreachable during this CI run rather than a code regression.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the most recent linuxptp-daemon commit is 0459bc0 (upstream-sync-2026-06-22) and the ptp-operator test repo shows 3586177 ("ci: add ginkgo flake mitigation and fix higher-priority test"). No log-format changes were observed that would break the regex. The failure is consistent with an infra/lab connectivity issue.
• Is it a flake? Yes — the cross-suite, cross-pod, cross-node uniformity of the timeout (all suites hit the same pattern) strongly indicates a transient infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, PTP network disruption in the telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com lab cluster) rather than a deterministic code regression. The oc-serial tests that ran later additionally hit Unauthorized / connection refused to the API server (10.8.34.117:6443), further confirming the lab cluster was degraded during this run.
• Suggested Fix: Re-run the nightly job to confir


TL;DR: Cluster log-stream collapse + API auth expiry wiped 22 of 24 tests; a linuxptp-daemon state-machine regression caused the remaining 2 TGM holdover failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 12/24 failures — linuxptp-daemon log stream unreachable (ClockSync GetProfileLogID/GetClockIDForeign timeout): All ClockSync tests in bc (3), dualfollower (3), dualnicbc (3), dualnicbcha (2), and oc-serial test 1 (1) hit could not find regex in log stream … error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded or timedout waiting for matches. The test helper opens a live kubectl logs --follow stream and waits for a ptp4l profile or sync line that never arrives within 3–10 minutes. Two compounding factors: (a) ptp4l may not be reaching SLAVE state cluster-wide (no grandmaster reachable or log format changed by PR #613), and (b) when the API server began degrading, streaming connections were silently severed rather than cleanly refused.

• 10/24 failures — Kubernetes API server Unauthorized mid-run (oc-serial tests 2–11): After the first oc-serial test completed at ~07:29 UTC, the kubeconfig credentials expired or the API server rejected them (Unauthorized / couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials). Every subsequent test aborted immediately at the DaemonSet readiness check (linuxptp-daemon DaemonSet must exist before readiness wait → Unauthorized). One variant also showed dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: connection refused, indicating the API server briefly went fully unreachable.

• 2/24 failures — TGM holdover state-machine regression (tgm suite): Both T-GM holdover tests fail deterministically: disabling GNSS causes ts2phcState to be forced to PTP_FREERUN (not PTP_HOLDOVER) when NoSourceTSCount == 2 in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/event/event.go:402–403, making ClockClass 7 unreachable. Test 1 exhausted its 3-minute poll; test 2 observed map[metric:248] (freerun) throughout the 10-second sampling window. This is a deterministic regression, not a flake.


Cross-Suite Patterns:


PatternSuites affected
GetProfileLogID / GetClockIDForeign log stream timeoutbc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, oc (test 1)
API server Unauthorized cascadeoc (tests 2–11)
GNSS → ClockClass 7 holdover state-machine bugtgm

The log-stream failures are 100% cross-suite (5 of 6 suites, identical error text, different pod names) — confirming a cluster-wide cause rather than a suite-specific issue. The oc Unauthorized failures are oc-specific but are a secondary consequence of the same cluster degradation event. The tgm failures are suite-specific and code-driven.


No suite is entirely clean. dualnicbcha is the only suite where the log-stream failure count is below its total suite size (2 of 2 failed; no "passing" baseline in that suite either).



Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job immediately and monitor the PTP grandmaster. The log-stream and API-auth failures bear all hallmarks of a transient lab infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, credential rotation, API server instability on telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com around 2026-06-24 07:00–08:30 UTC). A clean re-run will confirm whether the 22 non-TGM failures are infra flakes.

2. Audit linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0, "upstream-sync-2026-06-22") for ptp4l log-format changes. If the upstream sync altered the format of the Ptp4lConf: or selected best master clock log lines, the test regexes in ptphelper.go and pods.go will never match regardless of cluster health. Compare the ptp4l log output from a pre-PR-613 build against a post-PR-613 pod to confirm or rule out a log-format regression.

3. Fix the TGM holdover state machine in event.go:402–403. Remove or guard the unconditional ts2phcState = PTP_FREERUN override when NoSourceTSCount == 2; instead, allow the state to transition to PTP_HOLDOVER so the existing ClockClass 7 branch at lines 459–461 and 430–433 becomes reachable. This is a deterministic code regression and will not self-heal with a re-run.


Overall Issue Class: infra_other (dominant — 22/24 failures) with an embedded test_regression (2/24 tgm failures from PR #613 state-machine change)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — the entire 24-test job failed; the cluster experienced mid-run auth collapse, and a code regression in the TGM holdover path is deterministic and will recur on every re-run.




Per-Suite Details



bc



Suite: bc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests failed because Kubernetes log streaming to linuxptp-daemon pods returned context deadline exceeded / timeout errors during the GetProfileLogID step, preventing the test from locating the ptp4l config log line needed to derive the foreign master clock ID.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Kubernetes pod log stream failure in GetProfileLogID (affects: all 3 tests — "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-fpgx7 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

From the detailed agent logs (prior identical run same day, pod linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg):

```

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 1 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 2 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptptesthelper.go: 68] GetClockIDForeign retry due to err: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

Additionally, the API server was returning Unauthorized by 08:29 UTC (end of job), with the bc ClockSync tests running at 07:02–08:29 UTC — indicating progressive auth/credential degradation throughout the long 3.5-hour job:

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

E0624 08:29:47.118913 memcache.go:265] "Unhandled Error" err="couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials"

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetProfileLogID in test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go opens a live Kubernetes log stream (Follow: true, no TailLines) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex searching for the regex (?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: (.|\n)?message_tag \[([^\]]*)\] within a 3-minute timeout. The stream — opened with context.TODO() so no test-side deadline — is being terminated by the infrastructure with context deadline exceeded before the regex can be matched. This error pattern repeats identically across all ClockSync tests in bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, and dualnicbcha suites, confirming a cluster-wide log streaming connectivity issue rather than a daemon log format regression. The linuxptp-daemon does emit this log line (printNodeProfile in pkg/daemon/daemon.go:1369 writes the rendered Ptp4lConf with #profile: prefix and message_tag), but the HTTP connection carrying the pod log stream is dropped before the data reaches the test. The progressive Unauthorized failures at job end suggest the kubeconfig token was near expiry, which may also have disrupted API server proxy connections to node kubelets mid-run.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — no daemon code change identified; the failure is infrastructure-side log stream connectivity.
• Is it a flake? Yes
• Suggested Fix: Retry GetPodLogsRegex with exponential backoff on context deadline exceeded / stream errors (already partially attempted per ptphelper.go:123 retry log) and add a SinceSeconds window to avoid streaming large log volumes. Also investigate whether the telco5g bare-metal cluster's API server → kubelet log proxy connections are being cut by an intermediate timeout (check keepalive/idle settings on the cluster's internal load balancer).

Suite Issue Class: infra_timeout

Suite Severity: MEDIUM


dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the test helper GetProfileLogID could not find the Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1 log marker in linuxptp-daemon-9cv64's container logs — that entry was rotated out ~40 minutes before the tests ran.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Profile log entry lost to container log rotation (affects: all 3 tests — Slave can sync to master, Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down, Can provide a profile with higher priority)

• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded [tests 1 & 2]


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=timedout waiting for matches [test 3]

```

Test wall-clock timeouts (~201 s, ~205 s, ~207 s) are consistent with a 3-minute GetProfileLogID Pass-2 follow timeout (180 s) plus overhead. The dualfollower suite started at 05:45:01; the operator/daemon was deployed at ~05:05:33 — a gap of ~40 minutes.


The same failure pattern (could not get any profile line) hits every other suite in this run (bc → linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8/fpgx7; dualnicbc → linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q/4cmtj; dualnicbcha → linuxptp-daemon-8fk9k/mt258). All are cross-suite, cross-pod, and trigger the identical error path, confirming a systemic cause.


• Root Cause: BasicClockSyncCheck in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:60 calls GetClockIDForeign → GetProfileLogID (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:69), which scans linuxptp-daemon-container logs for the regex:

```

(?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1(.|\n)?message_tag \[(.*)\]

```

The daemon emits this line exactly once — inside applyNodePtpProfile → printNodeProfile → printWhenNotNil(nodeProfile.Ptp4lConf, "Ptp4lConf") at daemon.go:1369, called only when a ptpconfig is (re)applied. By 05:45, ptp4l + phc2sys have logged ~1 line/s for ~40 minutes; the early Ptp4lConf: entry has been rotated out of the container log visible to the Kubernetes GetLogs API. GetPodLogsRegex Pass 1 (snapshot, test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214) finds nothing; Pass 2 (follow, 3-minute context at pods.go:254) waits fruitlessly because the daemon never re-logs the profile until reconfigured, exhausting the timeout (pods.go:153 for tests 1–2, pods.go:167 for test 3), which bubbles up as ptphelper.go:83 "could not get any profile line".


• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the log-rotation exposure is a pre-existing test design limitation; no single PR is directly identifiable from available evidence. The most recent structural changes near this code path are 9be567c (2026-05-07, "refactor: Remove unused functions and enhance PTP configuration logic") and 0f98a60 (2026-01-14, "fixed ci blocker: added context timeout to GetLogsPodRegex") on the ptp-operator main branch; either could have affected how long Pass-1/Pass-2 tolerates missing entries. The release-4.20 branch merge history is not available locally to confirm backport.

• Is it a flake? No — all 3 tests in this suite failed, and the exact same pattern repeats across every other non-oc suite in the same run. This is a systematic failure.

• Suggested Fix: Change GetProfileLogID to periodically re-trigger the Ptp4lConf: log entry (e.g., by forcing a no-op ptpconfig update to restart reconciliation), or redesign the profile-ID lookup to not rely on a one-shot log event that may be rotated — for example, read it from the live PtpConfig CR spec and derive the messageTag from the known naming scheme (ptp4l..config:{level}), which is deterministic and does not require log scanning.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH

GetPodLogsRegex Pass 1 (snapshot, test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214) finds nothing; Pass 2 (follow, 3-minute context at pods.go:254) waits fruitlessly because the daemon never re-logs the profile until reconfigured, exhausting the timeout (pods.go:153 for tests 1–2, pods.go:167 for test 3), which bubbles up as ptphelper.go:83 "could not get any profile line".


• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the log-rotation exposure is a pre-existing test design limitation; no single PR is directly identifiable from available evidence. The most recent structural changes near this code path are 9be567c (2026-05-07, "refactor: Remove unused functions and enhance PTP configuration logic") and 0f98a60 (2026-01-14, "fixed ci blocker: added context timeout to GetLogsPodRegex") on the ptp-operator main branch; either could have affected how long Pass-1/Pass-2 tolerates missing entries. The release-4.20 branch merge history is not available locally to confirm backport.

• Is it a flake? No — all 3 tests in this suite failed, and the exact same pattern repeats across every other non-oc suite in the same run. This is a systematic failure.

• Suggested Fix: Change GetProfileLogID to periodically re-trigger the Ptp4lConf: log entry (e.g., by forcing a no-op ptpconfig update to restart reconciliation), or redesign the profile-ID lookup to not rely on a one-shot log event that may be rotated — for example, read it from the live PtpConfig CR spec and derive the messageTag from the known naming scheme (ptp4l..config:{level}), which is deterministic and does not require log scanning.

Suite Issue Class: test_failure

Suite Severity: HIGH


dualnicbc



Suite: dualnicbc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the linuxptp-daemon containers never emitted the selected best master clock log line, indicating PTP synchronization was never achieved on the test cluster nodes.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: linuxptp-daemon not achieving PTP clock synchronization (affects: "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-4cmtj container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches

```

And from the build log post-run (gathering phase):

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

error: creating temp namespace: Unauthorized

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetClockIDForeign() (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:127-151) scans the linuxptp-daemon-container log stream for the regex (?m)\[%s\]. selected best master clock (.) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex() (test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214-269), which internally calls findRegexInStream() (pods.go:141-171) with a 10-minute timeout. This line is only emitted by ptp4l when it successfully selects a grandmaster/best master; since it never appeared in any daemon pod across all ptpconfigs (test-bc-master1, test-slave1, temp), the PTP daemon was not achieving clock synchronization. Critically, the identical "could not find regex in log stream" error hit all ClockSync tests across bc-serial, dualfollower-serial, dualnicbcha-serial, and dualnicbc-serial as well — indicating a cluster-wide failure to synchronize PTP, most likely caused by the telco5g lab's physical grandmaster being unreachable during this CI run rather than a code regression.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the most recent linuxptp-daemon commit is 0459bc0 (upstream-sync-2026-06-22) and the ptp-operator test repo shows 3586177 ("ci: add ginkgo flake mitigation and fix higher-priority test"). No log-format changes were observed that would break the regex. The failure is consistent with an infra/lab connectivity issue.
• Is it a flake? Yes — the cross-suite, cross-pod, cross-node uniformity of the timeout (all suites hit the same pattern) strongly indicates a transient infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, PTP network disruption in the telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com lab cluster) rather than a deterministic code regression. The oc-serial tests that ran later additionally hit Unauthorized / connection refused to the API server (10.8.34.117:6443), further confirming the lab cluster was degraded during this run.
• Suggested Fix: Re-run the nightly job to confir


TL;DR: Cluster log-stream collapse + API auth expiry wiped 22 of 24 tests; a linuxptp-daemon state-machine regression caused the remaining 2 TGM holdover failures.



Root Cause Groups:


• 12/24 failures — linuxptp-daemon log stream unreachable (ClockSync GetProfileLogID/GetClockIDForeign timeout): All ClockSync tests in bc (3), dualfollower (3), dualnicbc (3), dualnicbcha (2), and oc-serial test 1 (1) hit could not find regex in log stream … error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded or timedout waiting for matches. The test helper opens a live kubectl logs --follow stream and waits for a ptp4l profile or sync line that never arrives within 3–10 minutes. Two compounding factors: (a) ptp4l may not be reaching SLAVE state cluster-wide (no grandmaster reachable or log format changed by PR #613), and (b) when the API server began degrading, streaming connections were silently severed rather than cleanly refused.

• 10/24 failures — Kubernetes API server Unauthorized mid-run (oc-serial tests 2–11): After the first oc-serial test completed at ~07:29 UTC, the kubeconfig credentials expired or the API server rejected them (Unauthorized / couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials). Every subsequent test aborted immediately at the DaemonSet readiness check (linuxptp-daemon DaemonSet must exist before readiness wait → Unauthorized). One variant also showed dial tcp 10.8.34.117:6443: connection refused, indicating the API server briefly went fully unreachable.

• 2/24 failures — TGM holdover state-machine regression (tgm suite): Both T-GM holdover tests fail deterministically: disabling GNSS causes ts2phcState to be forced to PTP_FREERUN (not PTP_HOLDOVER) when NoSourceTSCount == 2 in linuxptp-daemon/pkg/event/event.go:402–403, making ClockClass 7 unreachable. Test 1 exhausted its 3-minute poll; test 2 observed map[metric:248] (freerun) throughout the 10-second sampling window. This is a deterministic regression, not a flake.


Cross-Suite Patterns:


PatternSuites affected
GetProfileLogID / GetClockIDForeign log stream timeoutbc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, dualnicbcha, oc (test 1)
API server Unauthorized cascadeoc (tests 2–11)
GNSS → ClockClass 7 holdover state-machine bugtgm

The log-stream failures are 100% cross-suite (5 of 6 suites, identical error text, different pod names) — confirming a cluster-wide cause rather than a suite-specific issue. The oc Unauthorized failures are oc-specific but are a secondary consequence of the same cluster degradation event. The tgm failures are suite-specific and code-driven.


No suite is entirely clean. dualnicbcha is the only suite where the log-stream failure count is below its total suite size (2 of 2 failed; no "passing" baseline in that suite either).



Actionable Recommendations:


1. Re-run the job immediately and monitor the PTP grandmaster. The log-stream and API-auth failures bear all hallmarks of a transient lab infrastructure event (grandmaster unreachable, credential rotation, API server instability on telco5gran.eng.rdu2.redhat.com around 2026-06-24 07:00–08:30 UTC). A clean re-run will confirm whether the 22 non-TGM failures are infra flakes.

2. Audit linuxptp-daemon PR #613 (0459bc0, "upstream-sync-2026-06-22") for ptp4l log-format changes. If the upstream sync altered the format of the Ptp4lConf: or selected best master clock log lines, the test regexes in ptphelper.go and pods.go will never match regardless of cluster health. Compare the ptp4l log output from a pre-PR-613 build against a post-PR-613 pod to confirm or rule out a log-format regression.

3. Fix the TGM holdover state machine in event.go:402–403. Remove or guard the unconditional ts2phcState = PTP_FREERUN override when NoSourceTSCount == 2; instead, allow the state to transition to PTP_HOLDOVER so the existing ClockClass 7 branch at lines 459–461 and 430–433 becomes reachable. This is a deterministic code regression and will not self-heal with a re-run.


Overall Issue Class: infra_other (dominant — 22/24 failures) with an embedded test_regression (2/24 tgm failures from PR #613 state-machine change)


Overall Severity: CRITICAL — the entire 24-test job failed; the cluster experienced mid-run auth collapse, and a code regression in the TGM holdover path is deterministic and will recur on every re-run.




Per-Suite Details



bc



Suite: bc (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests failed because Kubernetes log streaming to linuxptp-daemon pods returned context deadline exceeded / timeout errors during the GetProfileLogID step, preventing the test from locating the ptp4l config log line needed to derive the foreign master clock ID.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Kubernetes pod log stream failure in GetProfileLogID (affects: all 3 tests — "Slave can sync to master", "Downstream slave can sync to BC master", "Can provide a profile with higher priority")
• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=timedout waiting for matches


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-fpgx7 container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

From the detailed agent logs (prior identical run same day, pod linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg):

```

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 1 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-5mcqg container=linuxptp-daemon-container, err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptphelper.go: 123] GetProfileLogID attempt 2 failed for test-bc-master1_test-bc-master1: ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded, retrying...

[ptptesthelper.go: 68] GetClockIDForeign retry due to err: could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream ... err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded

```

Additionally, the API server was returning Unauthorized by 08:29 UTC (end of job), with the bc ClockSync tests running at 07:02–08:29 UTC — indicating progressive auth/credential degradation throughout the long 3.5-hour job:

```

error: You must be logged in to the server (Unauthorized)

E0624 08:29:47.118913 memcache.go:265] "Unhandled Error" err="couldn't get current server API group list: the server has asked for the client to provide credentials"

```

• Root Cause: The test helper GetProfileLogID in test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go opens a live Kubernetes log stream (Follow: true, no TailLines) via pods.GetPodLogsRegex searching for the regex (?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: (.|\n)?message_tag \[([^\]]*)\] within a 3-minute timeout. The stream — opened with context.TODO() so no test-side deadline — is being terminated by the infrastructure with context deadline exceeded before the regex can be matched. This error pattern repeats identically across all ClockSync tests in bc, dualfollower, dualnicbc, and dualnicbcha suites, confirming a cluster-wide log streaming connectivity issue rather than a daemon log format regression. The linuxptp-daemon does emit this log line (printNodeProfile in pkg/daemon/daemon.go:1369 writes the rendered Ptp4lConf with #profile: prefix and message_tag), but the HTTP connection carrying the pod log stream is dropped before the data reaches the test. The progressive Unauthorized failures at job end suggest the kubeconfig token was near expiry, which may also have disrupted API server proxy connections to node kubelets mid-run.
• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — no daemon code change identified; the failure is infrastructure-side log stream connectivity.
• Is it a flake? Yes
• Suggested Fix: Retry GetPodLogsRegex with exponential backoff on context deadline exceeded / stream errors (already partially attempted per ptphelper.go:123 retry log) and add a SinceSeconds window to avoid streaming large log volumes. Also investigate whether the telco5g bare-metal cluster's API server → kubelet log proxy connections are being cut by an intermediate timeout (check keepalive/idle settings on the cluster's internal load balancer).

Suite Issue Class: infra_timeout

Suite Severity: MEDIUM


dualfollower



Suite: dualfollower (3 failures)


Suite TL;DR: All 3 ClockSync tests timed out because the test helper GetProfileLogID could not find the Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1 log marker in linuxptp-daemon-9cv64's container logs — that entry was rotated out ~40 minutes before the tests ran.


Root Cause Groups:


• Group 1: Profile log entry lost to container log rotation (affects: all 3 tests — Slave can sync to master, Dual follower can sync when one follower port goes down, Can provide a profile with higher priority)

• Evidence:

```

could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=error reading from stream: context deadline exceeded [tests 1 & 2]


could not get any profile line, err=could not find regex in log stream for

openshift-ptp/linuxptp-daemon-9cv64 container=linuxptp-daemon-container,

err=timedout waiting for matches [test 3]

```

Test wall-clock timeouts (~201 s, ~205 s, ~207 s) are consistent with a 3-minute GetProfileLogID Pass-2 follow timeout (180 s) plus overhead. The dualfollower suite started at 05:45:01; the operator/daemon was deployed at ~05:05:33 — a gap of ~40 minutes.


The same failure pattern (could not get any profile line) hits every other suite in this run (bc → linuxptp-daemon-hrsj8/fpgx7; dualnicbc → linuxptp-daemon-bvs6q/4cmtj; dualnicbcha → linuxptp-daemon-8fk9k/mt258). All are cross-suite, cross-pod, and trigger the identical error path, confirming a systemic cause.


• Root Cause: BasicClockSyncCheck in test/pkg/ptptesthelper/ptptesthelper.go:60 calls GetClockIDForeign → GetProfileLogID (test/pkg/ptphelper/ptphelper.go:69), which scans linuxptp-daemon-container logs for the regex:

```

(?m).?Ptp4lConf: #profile: test-slave1(.|\n)?message_tag \[(.*)\]

```

The daemon emits this line exactly once — inside applyNodePtpProfile → printNodeProfile → printWhenNotNil(nodeProfile.Ptp4lConf, "Ptp4lConf") at daemon.go:1369, called only when a ptpconfig is (re)applied. By 05:45, ptp4l + phc2sys have logged ~1 line/s for ~40 minutes; the early Ptp4lConf: entry has been rotated out of the container log visible to the Kubernetes GetLogs API. GetPodLogsRegex Pass 1 (snapshot, test/pkg/pods/pods.go:214) finds nothing; Pass 2 (follow, 3-minute context at pods.go:254) waits fruitlessly because the daemon never re-logs the profile until reconfigured, exhausting the timeout (pods.go:153 for tests 1–2, pods.go:167 for test 3), which bubbles up as ptphelper.go:83 "could not get any profile line".


• Breaking PR/Commit: Unknown — the log-rotation exposure is a pre-existing test design limitation; no single PR is directly identifiable from available evidence. The most recent structural changes near this code path are 9be567c (2026-05-07, "refactor: Remove unused functions and enhance PTP configuration logic") and 0f98a60 (2026-01-14, "fixed ci blocker: added context timeout to GetLogsPodRegex") on the ptp-operator main branch; either could have affected how long Pass-1/Pass-2 tolerates missing entries. The release-4.20 branch merge history is not available locally to confirm backport.

• Is it a flake? No — all 3 tests in this suite failed, and the exact same pattern repeats across every other non-oc suite in the same run. This is a systematic failure.

• Suggested Fix: Change GetProfileLogID to periodically re-trigger the Ptp4lConf: log entry (e.g., by forcing a no-op ptpconfig update to restart reconciliation), or redesign the profile-ID lookup to not rely on a one-shot log event that may be rotated — for example, read it from the live PtpConfig CR spec and derive the messageTag from the known naming scheme (ptp4l..config:{level}), which is deterministic and does not require log scanning.
